      <p>
       <small>
        <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_scopeA">
         <a href="#ref_scopeA">
          <b>
           <sup>
            A
           </sup>
          </b>
         </a>
        </span>
        Atlanta MSA in 2000 did not include Butts, Dawson, Haralson, Heard, Jasper, Lamar, Meriwether, and Price counties, whose population totalled in 2000: 135,783; in 2010: 156,368 (2.96% of total new 28-county metro)
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
         <a href="#cite_note-12">
          [12]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <br/>
        <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_relationB">
         <a href="#ref_relationB">
          <b>
           <sup>
            B
           </sup>
          </b>
         </a>
        </span>
        Compares the larger 28-county Atlanta-Sandy Springs-Marietta MSA 2010 with a smaller 20‑county Atlanta MSA 2000; however the 8 new counties represent less than 3% of the larger 28‑county metro.
        <br/>
        Source: for race and Hispanic population, U.S. Census Bureau 2010 and 2000 census; for foreign-born population: US Census Bureau 2010 and 2000 American Community Surveys;
        <a class="external text" href="http://wayback.archive-it.org/all/20120904134939/http://www.brookings.edu/~/media/files/rc/papers/2011/1013_immigration_wilson_singer/1013_immigration_wilson_singer.pdf" rel="nofollow">
         <i>
          Immigrants in 2010 Metropolitan America
         </i>
         , Brookings Institution
        </a>
       </small>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Race_and_ethnicity">
        Race and ethnicity
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Race and ethnicity">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/White_American" title="White American">
        White Americans
       </a>
       made up 55.4% of metro Atlanta's population, a relative decrease from 63.0% ten years earlier, but still an absolute increase of over 330,000 people. Non-Hispanic whites dropped from 59.5% to 50.7% of the metro's population, increasing by about 224,000 people.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_American" title="Black American">
        Black Americans
       </a>
       are the largest racial minority with 32.4% of the population, up from 28.9% in 2000. The city of Atlanta has long been regarded as a "
       <a href="/wiki/Black_mecca" title="Black mecca">
        black mecca
       </a>
       " for its role as a center of black education, political power, wealth, and culture. From 2000 to 2010, the geographic distribution of blacks in Metro Atlanta changed radically. Long concentrated in the city of Atlanta and DeKalb County, the black population there dropped as more than half a million African Americans settled across other parts of the metro area, including approximately 112,000 in Gwinnett County, 71,000 in Fulton outside Atlanta, 58,000 in Cobb, 50,000 in Clayton, 34,000 in Douglas, and 27,000 each in Newton and Rockdale counties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Due to its availability of jobs, Atlanta has been a destination for young college-educated blacks in the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Great_Migration" title="New Great Migration">
        Reverse Great Migration
       </a>
       of African Americans from the North since the turn of the 21st century, with many settling quickly into suburban locations.
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th>
         Year
        </th>
        <th>
         Black pop. in
         <br/>
         City of Atlanta
        </th>
        <th>
         Black pop. in
         <br/>
         DeKalb County
        </th>
        <th>
         Total black pop.
         <br/>
         Atlanta + DeKalb
        </th>
        <th>
         Total black pop.
         <br/>
         Metro Atlanta
        </th>
        <th>
         Proportion of black pop.
         <br/>
         in Atlanta + DeKalb
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         2000
        </td>
        <td>
         255,689
        </td>
        <td>
         361,111
        </td>
        <td>
         616,800
        </td>
        <td>
         1,189,179
        </td>
        <td>
         51.9%
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         2010
        </td>
        <td>
         226,894
        </td>
        <td>
         375,697
        </td>
        <td>
         602,591
        </td>
        <td>
         1,707,913
        </td>
        <td>
         35.2%
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_and_Latino_Americans" title="Hispanic and Latino Americans">
        Hispanic Americans
       </a>
       are the fastest growing ethnic group. At 10.4% of the metro's population in 2010, versus only 6.5% in 2000, the metro's Hispanic population increased an astounding 109.6%, or 298,459 people, in ten years. Major Hispanic groups include 354,351
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_American" title="Mexican American">
        Mexicans
       </a>
       , 43,337
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_American" title="Puerto Rican American">
        Puerto Ricans
       </a>
       and 17,648
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_American" title="Cuban American">
        Cubans
       </a>
       . All of those groups' populations increased by over 90% in the ten-year period. Of the metro's 299,000-person increase in the Hispanic population from 2000 to 2010, 98,000 came in Gwinnett County, 57,000 in Cobb, 55,000 in Fulton (all but 3,000 outside the city of Atlanta), 20,000 in Hall, and 15,000 in DeKalb County.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asian_American" title="Asian American">
        Asian American
       </a>
       population also increased rapidly from 2000 to 2010. There were 296,956 Asian-Americans in the metro area in 2010, making up 5.9% of the population. This represented an 87% increase over 2000. The largest Asian groups are 108,980
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_American" title="Indian American">
        Indians
       </a>
       , 93,870
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_American" title="Korean American">
        Korean Americans
       </a>
       , 67,660 Chinese, and 66,554 Vietnamese.
      </p>
      <p>
       Atlanta also has Georgia's largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bosnian_American" title="Bosnian American">
        Bosnian American
       </a>
       population with approximately 10,000 in the metro area, mainly in Gwinnett County
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Metro Atlanta is increasingly international, with its 716,434 foreign-born residents in 2010, a 69% increase versus 2000. This was the fourth largest rate of growth among the nation's top 100 metros, after
       <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">
        Baltimore
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orlando" title="Orlando">
        Orlando
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">
        Las Vegas
       </a>
       . The foreign-born proportion of the population went up from 10.3% to 13.6%, and Atlanta moved up from 14th to 12th in ranking of U.S. metro areas with the largest immigrant population by sheer numbers. Still, its 13.6% proportion of immigrants is only the 29th highest of the nation's top 100 metros.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brookings2011_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-brookings2011-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Metro Atlanta's immigrants are more suburban than those of most cities. Out of the top 100 U.S. metros, Atlanta has the 11th highest ratio of the foreign-born living in the suburbs and not in the core city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-brookings2011_16-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-brookings2011-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Atlanta has a few
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_enclave" title="Ethnic enclave">
        ethnic enclaves
       </a>
       such as a
       <a href="/wiki/Koreatown" title="Koreatown">
        Koreatown
       </a>
       , and areas such as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buford_Highway_Corridor" title="Buford Highway Corridor">
        Buford Highway Corridor
       </a>
       in DeKalb County and parts of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gwinnett_County" title="Gwinnett County">
        Gwinnett County
       </a>
       are commercial centers for multiple ethnic communities.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1990 Greater Atlanta had the largest Japanese population in the Southeast United States. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Consulate_General_of_Japan_in_Atlanta" title="Consulate General of Japan in Atlanta">
        Consulate General of Japan in Atlanta
       </a>
       estimated that, during that year, 7,500 to 10,000 Japanese lived in Greater Atlanta. Of the metropolitan areas in the Southeast United States, as of 1990 Greater Atlanta had the most extensive education network for Japanese nationals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lively_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Lively-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
        Language
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Language">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In 2008, approximately 83.3% of the population five years and older spoke only
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       at home, which is roughly 4,125,000 people. Over 436,000 people (8.8%) spoke
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       at home, giving Metro Atlanta the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._cities_by_Spanish-speaking_population" title="List of U.S. cities by Spanish-speaking population">
        15th highest number of Spanish speakers
       </a>
       among American metropolitan areas (MSAs). Over 193,000 people (3.9%) spoke other Indo-European languages at home. People who speak an
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Asia" title="Languages of Asia">
        Asian language
       </a>
       at home numbered over 137,000 and made up 2.8% of the population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Atlanta" title="Economy of Atlanta">
        Economy of Metro Atlanta
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities">
        Utilities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Utilities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The area is the world's largest toll-free calling zone spanning 7,162 square miles (18,549 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       has four active
       <a href="/wiki/Telephone" title="Telephone">
        telephone
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Telephone_numbering_plan" title="Telephone numbering plan">
        area codes
       </a>
       , and local calling extending into portions of two others.
       <a href="/wiki/Area_code_404" title="Area code 404">
        404
       </a>
       , which originally covered all of northern
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">
        Georgia
       </a>
       until 1992, now covers mostly the area inside the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perimeter_(Atlanta)" title="Perimeter (Atlanta)">
        Perimeter
       </a>
       (Interstate 285). In 1995 the
       <a href="/wiki/Suburb" title="Suburb">
        suburbs
       </a>
       were put into
       <a href="/wiki/Area_code_770" title="Area code 770">
        770
       </a>
       , requiring mandatory ten‑digit dialing even for local calls under
       <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">
        FCC
       </a>
       rules. This made Atlanta one of the US's first cities to employ
       <a href="/wiki/Ten-digit_dialing" title="Ten-digit dialing">
        ten-digit dialing
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which was begun by
       <a href="/wiki/BellSouth" title="BellSouth">
        BellSouth
       </a>
       the year before the Centennial
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1996_Olympic_Games" title="1996 Olympic Games">
        1996 Olympic Games
       </a>
       . In 1998,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_678" title="Area code 678">
        678
       </a>
       was overlaid onto both of the existing 404 and 770 area codes.
       <a href="/wiki/Mobile_phone" title="Mobile phone">
        Mobile phones
       </a>
       , originally only assigned to 404, may now have any local area code regardless of where in the region they were issued.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_470" title="Area code 470">
        Area code 470
       </a>
       , the newest area code, was overlaid with 404 and 770 in the same fashion as 678. The local calling area also includes portions of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_706" title="Area code 706">
        706/762
       </a>
       and a small area of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Area_code_256" title="Area code 256">
        256
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Alabama" title="Alabama">
        Alabama
       </a>
       on the Georgia border.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The city of Atlanta is the most wired city in the United States.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many residents access the internet on a high-speed broadband and/or WiFi connection. It is home to one of the world's largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiber-optic" title="Fiber-optic">
        fiber-optic
       </a>
       bundles.
      </p>
      <p>
       Major
       <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">
        petroleum
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_transport" title="Pipeline transport">
        pipelines
       </a>
       cross the area, running from the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">
        Gulf
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Coast" title="Coast">
        coast
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">
        Texas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       to the population centers of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northeastern_U.S." title="Northeastern U.S.">
        northeastern U.S.
       </a>
       This includes
       <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Pipeline" title="Colonial Pipeline">
        Colonial Pipeline
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plantation_Pipe_Line&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plantation Pipe Line (page does not exist)">
        Plantation Pipe Line
       </a>
       , both based in Alpharetta.
      </p>
      <p>
       Metro Atlanta primarily uses
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Central_heating" title="Central heating">
        central heating
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_heater" title="Water heater">
        water heaters
       </a>
       , with the major exception of
       <a href="/wiki/Heat_pump" title="Heat pump">
        heat pumps
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Apartment" title="Apartment">
        apartments
       </a>
       built during and since the 1980s. This is because winters are mild, and large apartment buildings usually require little energy to heat. Backup heat (also used during
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defrost" title="Defrost">
        defrosting
       </a>
       ) is usually supplied by electric
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resistance_heating" title="Resistance heating">
        resistance heating
       </a>
       , though some homes have
       <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_heat" title="Hybrid heat">
        hybrid heating
       </a>
       units which use gas backup when it is cold. Exurban homes may also use all-electric instead of gas, if
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_main" title="Gas main">
        gas mains
       </a>
       have not been extended to an area.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cooktop" title="Cooktop">
        Cooktops
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Oven" title="Oven">
        ovens
       </a>
       are a mix of gas and electric, while gas
       <a href="/wiki/Clothes_dryer" title="Clothes dryer">
        clothes dryers
       </a>
       are rather rare. Nearly all homes have a
       <a href="/wiki/Fireplace" title="Fireplace">
        fireplace
       </a>
       with a manual-
       <a href="/wiki/Valve" title="Valve">
        valve
       </a>
       gas starter, and some are now equipped with permanent
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gas_log&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gas log (page does not exist)">
        gas logs
       </a>
       with
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_fireplace" title="Electric fireplace">
        electric switch start
       </a>
       . Some homes also have natural gas
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grill_(cooking)" title="Grill (cooking)">
        barbecue grills
       </a>
       , formerly sold at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Utility_company" title="Utility company">
        utility company
       </a>
       stores.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Power" title="Georgia Power">
        Georgia Power
       </a>
       is the main
       <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">
        electric power
       </a>
       company across the state and the metro area, beginning in 1902 as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_Railway_and_Power_Company" title="Georgia Railway and Power Company">
        Georgia Railway and Power Company
       </a>
       , Atlanta's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streetcar" title="Streetcar">
        streetcar
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">
        trolley
       </a>
       ) company. Several
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electric_membership_corporation" title="Electric membership corporation">
        electric membership corporations
       </a>
       also serve the suburbs. These include the second-largest EMC in the nation
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Jackson_Electric_Membership_Corporation" title="Jackson Electric Membership Corporation">
        Jackson EMC
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cobb_EMC" title="Cobb EMC">
        Cobb EMC
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sawnee_EMC&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sawnee EMC (page does not exist)">
        Sawnee EMC
       </a>
       . The city of Marietta operates its own electric utility,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Marietta_Power&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Marietta Power (page does not exist)">
        Marietta Power
       </a>
       , under the Board of Lights &amp; Water (BLW). It is also a member of the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Municipal_Electric_Association_of_Georgia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Municipal Electric Association of Georgia (page does not exist)">
        Municipal Electric Association of Georgia
       </a>
       (MEAG).
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Gas_Light" title="Atlanta Gas Light">
        Atlanta Gas Light
       </a>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">
        natural gas
       </a>
       utility for the region, and has been so for over a
       <a href="/wiki/Century" title="Century">
        century
       </a>
       and a half, since it installed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_lamp" title="Gas lamp">
        gas lamps
       </a>
       in Atlanta in 1856. It operated as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regulated_monopoly" title="Regulated monopoly">
        regulated monopoly
       </a>
       until November 1998, the after the state legislature voted in early 1997 to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deregulate" title="Deregulate">
        deregulate
       </a>
       natural gas
       <a href="/wiki/Marketing" title="Marketing">
        marketing
       </a>
       , and make customers choose among nearly 20 different marketers still selling the same AGL-
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wholesale" title="Wholesale">
        wholesaled
       </a>
       gas, such as
       <a class="external text" href="http://www.gas-south.com/" rel="nofollow">
        Gas South
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="external text" href="https://www.infiniteenergy.com/" rel="nofollow">
        Infinite Energy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/SCANA" title="SCANA">
        SCANA
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_Natural_Gas" title="Georgia Natural Gas">
        Georgia Natural Gas
       </a>
       . Most of the gas comes via
       <a href="/wiki/Pipeline_transport" title="Pipeline transport">
        pipeline
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Louisiana" title="Louisiana">
        Louisiana
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Water is provided by various county and a few city systems. Several of these systems actually serve parts of neighboring counties and cities as well. The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cobb-Marietta_Water_Authority&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cobb-Marietta Water Authority (page does not exist)">
        Cobb-Marietta Water Authority
       </a>
       serves not only Cobb, but also parts of neighboring Paulding and Cherokee counties, for example. During
       <a href="/wiki/Drought" title="Drought">
        drought
       </a>
       or other
       <a href="/wiki/Emergency" title="Emergency">
        emergency
       </a>
       , cities and counties can enact
       <a href="/wiki/Outdoor_water-use_restriction" title="Outdoor water-use restriction">
        outdoor water-use restrictions
       </a>
       , however some cross-
       <a href="/wiki/Jurisdiction" title="Jurisdiction">
        jurisdiction
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Water_system" title="Water system">
        water systems
       </a>
       have also acted to put bans in place. In late September 2007, the state
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Environmental_Protection_Division&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Environmental Protection Division (page does not exist)">
        Environmental Protection Division
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Department_of_Natural_Resources" title="Georgia Department of Natural Resources">
        Georgia Department of Natural Resources
       </a>
       , stepped-in with its first-ever ban, covering most of the northern half of the state. While
       <a href="/wiki/Surface_water" title="Surface water">
        surface water
       </a>
       is by far the primary source of water for the region, the drought had many systems (and a few wealthy homeowners) drilling new
       <a href="/wiki/Water_well" title="Water well">
        wells
       </a>
       for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ground_water" title="Ground water">
        ground water
       </a>
       , though the local
       <a href="/wiki/Water_table" title="Water table">
        water table
       </a>
       is around 400 feet (120 m) deep, on
       <a href="/wiki/Average" title="Average">
        average
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_sewer" title="Sanitary sewer">
        Sewerage
       </a>
       is also handled by the water utilities, however the various water and sewer networks may not conform to the same boundaries, resulting in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interbasin_water_transfer" title="Interbasin water transfer">
        interbasin water transfers
       </a>
       . This is for practical reasons, because the area is hilly and divided by several
       <a href="/wiki/Drainage_divide" title="Drainage divide">
        watersheds
       </a>
       , because the area has developed irregularly and erratically, and because
       <a href="/wiki/Water_treatment" title="Water treatment">
        water treatment
       </a>
       plants are usually not near
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sewage_treatment_plant" title="Sewage treatment plant">
        sewage treatment plants
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Septic_tank" title="Septic tank">
        Septic tanks
       </a>
       are still used in the older homes of some exurbs.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">
        Housing
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Housing">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Low-density
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Residential_subdivision" title="Residential subdivision">
        residential subdivision
       </a>
       development dominates the metro Atlanta suburbs.
      </p>
      <p>
       Changes in
       <a href="/wiki/House_price_index" title="House price index">
        house prices
       </a>
       for the metro area are publicly tracked on a regular basis using the
       <a href="/wiki/Case%E2%80%93Shiller_index" title="Case–Shiller index">
        Case–Shiller index
       </a>
       ; the statistic is published by
       <a href="/wiki/Standard_%26_Poor%27s" title="Standard &amp; Poor's">
        Standard &amp; Poor's
       </a>
       and is also a component of S&amp;P's 20‑city
       <a href="/wiki/Composite_(finance)" title="Composite (finance)">
        composite index
       </a>
       of the value of the U.S. residential real estate market.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Community_improvement_districts">
        Community improvement districts
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Community improvement districts">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       All of Georgia's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Community_improvement_district" title="Community improvement district">
        community improvement districts
       </a>
       are located in metro Atlanta.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Buckhead_Community_Improvement_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Buckhead Community Improvement District (page does not exist)">
         Buckhead Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , covering
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buckhead_(Atlanta)" title="Buckhead (Atlanta)">
         Buckhead
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
         <a href="#cite_note-25">
          [25]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Perimeter_Center_Community_Improvement_Districts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Perimeter Center Community Improvement Districts (page does not exist)">
         Perimeter Center Community Improvement Districts
        </a>
        , covering the
        <a href="/wiki/Perimeter_Center" title="Perimeter Center">
         Perimeter Center
        </a>
        area of Sandy Springs and Dunwoody
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
         <a href="#cite_note-26">
          [26]
         </a>
        </sup>
        /
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Community_Improvement_District" title="Cumberland Community Improvement District">
         Cumberland Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , around
        <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Mall" title="Cumberland Mall">
         Cumberland Mall
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
         <a href="#cite_note-27">
          [27]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Town_Center_Area_Community_Improvement_District" title="Town Center Area Community Improvement District">
         Town Center Area Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , around
        <a href="/wiki/Town_Center_at_Cobb" title="Town Center at Cobb">
         Town Center at Cobb
        </a>
        mall
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
         <a href="#cite_note-28">
          [28]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gwinnett_Place_Community_Improvement_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gwinnett Place Community Improvement District (page does not exist)">
         Gwinnett Place Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , around
        <a href="/wiki/Gwinnett_Place_Mall" title="Gwinnett Place Mall">
         Gwinnett Place Mall
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
         <a href="#cite_note-29">
          [29]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gwinnett_Village_Community_Improvement_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gwinnett Village Community Improvement District (page does not exist)">
         Gwinnett Village Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , also in Gwinnett county southeast of Norcross
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
         <a href="#cite_note-30">
          [30]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Evermore_Community_Improvement_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Evermore Community Improvement District (page does not exist)">
         Evermore Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , or
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Highway_78_Community_Improvement_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Highway 78 Community Improvement District (page does not exist)">
         Highway 78 Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , covering part of the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._78" title="U.S. 78">
         U.S. 78
        </a>
        corridor in Gwinnett near
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snellville" title="Snellville">
         Snellville
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
         <a href="#cite_note-31">
          [31]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lilburn_Community_Improvement_District&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lilburn Community Improvement District (page does not exist)">
         Lilburn Community Improvement District
        </a>
        , established early 2010 in
        <a href="/wiki/Lilburn,_Georgia" title="Lilburn, Georgia">
         Lilburn
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Aerotropolis Atlanta CIDs
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
         <a href="#cite_note-32">
          [32]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Boulevard CID (industrial district), created 2010
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
         <a href="#cite_note-33">
          [33]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In May 2016, the City of Atlanta launched Atlanta City Studio, the city's first "pop-up urban design laboratory focused on shaping the future of city neighborhoods."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The studio hosts "lectures, open forums, urban art presentations and other neighborhood and design components."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Atlanta City Studio will relocate twice per year in order for residents to interact with staff and share their ideas about improving city design. The studio is located on the second floor of
       <a href="/wiki/Ponce_City_Market" title="Ponce City Market">
        Ponce City Market
       </a>
       and in January 2017 will relocate "to a retail location on the Westside, possibly on MLK Jr. Drive or Cascade Road."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_colleges_and_universities">
        Major colleges and universities
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Major colleges and universities">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta,_Georgia" title="Atlanta, Georgia">
        Atlanta, Georgia
       </a>
       is home to the largest concentration of colleges and universities in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_United_States" title="Southern United States">
        Southern United States
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_metropolitan_Atlanta" title="List of colleges and universities in metropolitan Atlanta">
        List of major colleges and universities in metropolitan Atlanta
       </a>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_University_Center" title="Atlanta University Center">

        </a>

          </a>
         </li>
         <li>

          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Spelman_College" title="Spelman College">

          </a>
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Interdenominational_Theological_Center" title="Interdenominational Theological Center">

         </li>

          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Agnes_Scott_College" title="Agnes Scott College">

        </a>
       </li>
       <li>

        </a>
       </li>
       <li>

        </a>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">
        Healthcare
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Healthcare">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The area is served by a network of healthcare facilities including private practice, urgent care, hospital systems, and specialty care facilities. There are approximately 28 hospitals serving the metro. There are both private for profit systems and community not-for-profit systems.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Major_healthcare_systems">
        Major healthcare systems
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>

        Culture and attractions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Culture and attractions">

      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Atlanta" title="Sports in Atlanta">
        Sports in Atlanta
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Atlanta metropolitan area hosts five major league sports franchises: the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Hawks" title="Atlanta Hawks">
        Atlanta Hawks
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
        National Basketball Association
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Dream" title="Atlanta Dream">
        Atlanta Dream
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_National_Basketball_Association" title="Women's National Basketball Association">
        Women's National Basketball Association
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons" title="Atlanta Falcons">
        Atlanta Falcons
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">
        National Football League
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">
        Atlanta Braves
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">
        Major League Baseball
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_United_FC" title="Atlanta United FC">
        Atlanta United FC
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">
        Major League Soccer
       </a>
       . Atlanta also plays host one
       <a href="/wiki/Monster_Energy_NASCAR_Cup_Series" title="Monster Energy NASCAR Cup Series">
        Monster Energy NASCAR Cup Series
       </a>
       race each year.
      </p>
      <p>
       Former teams include the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Flames" title="Atlanta Flames">
        Atlanta Flames
       </a>
       (now
       <a href="/wiki/Calgary_Flames" title="Calgary Flames">
        Calgary Flames
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Thrashers" title="Atlanta Thrashers">
        Atlanta Thrashers
       </a>
       (now
       <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg_Jets" title="Winnipeg Jets">
        Winnipeg Jets
       </a>
       ), both of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
        National Hockey League
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       For minor league franchises, the Atlanta metropolitan area is home to the
       <a href="/wiki/Gwinnett_Stripers" title="Gwinnett Stripers">
        Gwinnett Stripers
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Triple-A_(baseball)" title="Triple-A (baseball)">
        Triple-A
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">
        International League
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Lawrenceville,_Georgia" title="Lawrenceville, Georgia">
        Lawrenceville
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Gladiators" title="Atlanta Gladiators">
        Atlanta Gladiators
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/ECHL" title="ECHL">
        ECHL
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Duluth,_Georgia" title="Duluth, Georgia">
        Duluth
       </a>
       . Starting in 2019,
       <a href="/wiki/College_Park,_Georgia" title="College Park, Georgia">
        College Park
       </a>
       will be home of the Hawks'
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_Development_League" title="NBA Development League">
        NBA G-League
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Erie_BayHawks_(2017%E2%80%93)" title="Erie BayHawks (2017–)">
        franchise
       </a>
       ; the team is currently based in
       <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">
        Erie, Pennsylvania
       </a>
       while an arena is under construction at the
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_International_Convention_Center" title="Georgia International Convention Center">
        Georgia International Convention Center
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Atlanta metropolitan area is also home to three
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">
        NCAA Division I
       </a>
       programs, with the
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Tech_Yellow_Jackets" title="Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets">
        Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_State_Panthers" title="Georgia State Panthers">
        Georgia State Panthers
       </a>
       in Atlanta proper and the
       <a href="/wiki/Kennesaw_State_Owls" title="Kennesaw State Owls">
        Kennesaw State Owls
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Kennesaw,_Georgia" title="Kennesaw, Georgia">
        Kennesaw
       </a>
       . Both Georgia Tech and Georgia State are members of the
       <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Football_Bowl_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I Football Bowl Subdivision">
        Football Bowl Subdivision
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Coast_Conference" title="Atlantic Coast Conference">
        Atlantic Coast Conference
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Sun_Belt_Conference" title="Sun Belt Conference">
        Sun Belt Conference
       </a>
       , respectively, while Kennesaw State is a football member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Big_South_Conference" title="Big South Conference">
        Big South Conference
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I#Football_Championship_Subdivision" title="NCAA Division I">
        Football Championship Subdivision
       </a>
       while its remaining sports are in the non-football
       <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Sun_Conference" title="Atlantic Sun Conference">
        Atlantic Sun Conference
       </a>
       .
      </p>
