      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transit_systems">
        Transit systems
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Transit systems">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Atlanta has always been a mail town, and the city once had an extensive
       <a href="/wiki/Streetcars_in_Atlanta" title="Streetcars in Atlanta">
        streetcar
       </a>
       system, which also provided
       <a href="/wiki/Interurban" title="Interurban">
        interurban
       </a>
       service as far out as Marietta, 15 miles (24 km) to the northwest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The streetcars were replaced by an extensive
       <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Atlanta" title="Trolleybuses in Atlanta">
        trolleybus system
       </a>
       , supplemented by buses, in the 1940s and 1950–52, and then converted to all buses in the 1950s and 1960-62. However, building a modern rapid transit system proved a difficult and drawn-out process and, compared to the original plans for a regional system, has only partially been accomplished.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Atlanta_Rapid_Transit_Authority" title="Metropolitan Atlanta Rapid Transit Authority">
        MARTA
       </a>
       operates buses and a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subway_system" title="Subway system">
        subway system
       </a>
       in the city of Atlanta, Fulton, Clayton and Dekalb counties, while
       <a href="/wiki/Cobb_Community_Transit" title="Cobb Community Transit">
        Cobb
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gwinnett_County_Transit" title="Gwinnett County Transit">
        Gwinnett
       </a>
       counties operate their own independent Suburban Transit Systems that feed into MARTA. This is a result of those counties' refusal to join the MARTA system, a situation which was originally closely related to
       <a href="/wiki/White_flight" title="White flight">
        white flight
       </a>
       from the city.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is the only US system in which the state does not provide any funds for operation or expansion, instead relying entirely on a 1%
       <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">
        sales tax
       </a>
       in its three counties. Due to the passage of a 1% sales tax in Clayton County on November 4, 2014, MARTA replaced the defunct C-Tran system bringing buses and commuter rail to the county beginning March 2015, with full bus service in 2016. The
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Streetcar" title="Atlanta Streetcar">
        Atlanta Streetcar
       </a>
       , a 2.7-mile (4.3 km) light rail loop, connects
       <a href="/wiki/Centennial_Olympic_Park" title="Centennial Olympic Park">
        Centennial Olympic Park
       </a>
       and MARTA heavy rail subway to the Sweet Auburn district and points in between.
       <a href="/wiki/GRTA_Xpress" title="GRTA Xpress">
        Xpress GA
       </a>
       , a suburban commuter bus service operated by the Georgia Regional Transportation Authority or GRTA, has over 32 routes running from the suburbs and exurbs to downtown Atlanta in 12 metropolitan counties.
      </p>
      <p>
       Plans are underway for commuter rail and
       <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">
        bus rapid transit
       </a>
       (BRT), though these are some years away. The $20 billion
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwest_Corridor_HOV/BRT" title="Northwest Corridor HOV/BRT">
        Northwest Corridor HOV/BRT
       </a>
       project appears to conflict with other plans, such as the metro-wide
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Concept_3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Concept 3 (page does not exist)">
        Concept 3
       </a>
       approved by the
       <a href="/wiki/Transit_Planning_Board" title="Transit Planning Board">
        Transit Planning Board
       </a>
       , and the no-
       <a href="/wiki/Jersey_barrier" title="Jersey barrier">
        barrier
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/High-occupancy_toll_lane" title="High-occupancy toll lane">
        HOT lanes
       </a>
       on I‑85 in Gwinnett. MARTA is also considering a BRT line of its own to the east.
      </p>
      <p>
       The first
       <a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail" title="Commuter rail">
        commuter rail
       </a>
       line would run south of the city, eventually extended to
       <a href="/wiki/Lovejoy,_Georgia" title="Lovejoy, Georgia">
        Lovejoy
       </a>
       and possibly
       <a href="/wiki/Hampton,_Georgia" title="Hampton, Georgia">
        Hampton
       </a>
       near
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Motor_Speedway" title="Atlanta Motor Speedway">
        Atlanta Motor Speedway
       </a>
       . The "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brain_Train" title="Brain Train">
        Brain Train
       </a>
       " would likely be the second route, connecting the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Georgia" title="University of Georgia">
        University of Georgia
       </a>
       in Athens to
       <a href="/wiki/Emory_University" title="Emory University">
        Emory University
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_Tech" title="Georgia Tech">
        Georgia Tech
       </a>
       in Atlanta.
      </p>
      <p>
       As planned, all commuter trains would arrive at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlanta_Multimodal_Passenger_Terminal" title="Atlanta Multimodal Passenger Terminal">
        Atlanta Multimodal Passenger Terminal
       </a>
       (MMPT), the long-delayed facility just across
       <a href="/wiki/Peachtree_Street" title="Peachtree Street">
        Peachtree Street
       </a>
       from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Five_Points_(MARTA_station)" title="Five Points (MARTA station)">
        Five Points MARTA station
       </a>
       , where all of its lines meet. Planning for the system and its extension as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intercity_rail" title="Intercity rail">
        intercity rail
       </a>
       across the state are the responsibility of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_Rail_Passenger_Authority" title="Georgia Rail Passenger Authority">
        Georgia Rail Passenger Authority
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Another proposed plan that has received very strong
       <a href="/wiki/Grassroots" title="Grassroots">
        grassroots
       </a>
       support in recent years is the
       <a href="/wiki/BeltLine" title="BeltLine">
        BeltLine
       </a>
       , a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenbelt" title="Greenbelt">
        greenbelt
       </a>
       and transit system that takes advantage of existing and unused rail tracks to set up a 22-mile (35 km)
       <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">
        light rail
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Streetcar" title="Streetcar">
        streetcar
       </a>
       circuit around the core of Atlanta, as well as establishing more
       <a href="/wiki/Open_space_reserve" title="Open space reserve">
        green space
       </a>
       and footpaths for pedestrians and bicyclists.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_railways">
        Commercial railways
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Commercial railways">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Before Atlanta was even a city, it was a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Railroad" title="Railroad">
        railroad
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_hub" title="Transport hub">
        hub
       </a>
       . From this came the joke, popular among other
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Southern_U.S._culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Southern U.S. culture (page does not exist)">
        Southerners
       </a>
       , that "regardless of whether one goes to
       <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">
        heaven
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Hell" title="Hell">
        hell
       </a>
       , everyone must go through Atlanta first". Many of its suburbs pre-date it as depots or
       <a href="/wiki/Train_station" title="Train station">
        train stations
       </a>
       along the major lines in and out of town.
      </p>
      <p>
       Many of these
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historic" title="Historic">
        historic
       </a>
       stations, including Atlanta's
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta_Union_Station_(1930)" title="Atlanta Union Station (1930)">
        Union Station
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Terminal_Station_(Atlanta)" title="Terminal Station (Atlanta)">
        Terminal Station
       </a>
       , were
       <a href="/wiki/Demolition" title="Demolition">
        demolished
       </a>
       like many county
       <a href="/wiki/Courthouse" title="Courthouse">
        courthouses
       </a>
       and other historic buildings. Many have been saved however, including the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%26N" title="L&amp;N">
        L&amp;N
       </a>
       station in Woodstock, and the stations along the main
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/W%26A" title="W&amp;A">
        W&amp;A
       </a>
       line in Marietta and Smyrna.
      </p>
      <p>
       Through
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merger" title="Merger">
        mergers
       </a>
       , the main railroads in the area are now
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norfolk_Southern" title="Norfolk Southern">
        Norfolk Southern
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CSX" title="CSX">
        CSX
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Northeastern_Railroad" title="Georgia Northeastern Railroad">
        Georgia Northeastern Railroad
       </a>
       is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short-line_railroad" title="Short-line railroad">
        short line
       </a>
       that also services part of the area. There are also several
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Railyards_of_Atlanta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Railyards of Atlanta (page does not exist)">
        railyards of Atlanta
       </a>
       and vicinity, as well as the
       <a href="/wiki/Southeastern_Railway_Museum" title="Southeastern Railway Museum">
        Southeastern Railway Museum
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Southern_Museum_of_Civil_War_and_Locomotive_History" title="Southern Museum of Civil War and Locomotive History">
        Southern Museum of Civil War and Locomotive History
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The National Railroad Passenger Corporation, more commonly known as
       <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">
        Amtrak
       </a>
       , runs the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intercity_rail" title="Intercity rail">
        intercity rail
       </a>
       line
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crescent_(Amtrak)" title="Crescent (Amtrak)">
        Crescent
       </a>
       through metro Atlanta twice daily, with one train heading towards
       <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">
        New Orleans
       </a>
       and the other headed towards
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_(city)" title="New York (city)">
        New York
       </a>
       . All trains make a scheduled stop at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peachtree_Station" title="Peachtree Station">
        Peachtree Station
       </a>
       in northern Midtown Atlanta, but it is also possible for arrange for trains to stop in
       <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Georgia" title="Gainesville, Georgia">
        Gainesville
       </a>
       , Georgia as well.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Air">
        Air
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Air">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hartsfield-Jackson_Atlanta_International_Airport" title="Hartsfield-Jackson Atlanta International Airport">
        Hartsfield-Jackson Atlanta International Airport
       </a>
       is the only
       <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">
        international airport
       </a>
       for the region (and only major international airport for the state), and as with rail travel, it became the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ubiquitous" title="Ubiquitous">
        ubiquitous
       </a>
       place through which everyone must travel at some point.
       <a href="/wiki/Atlanta%27s_second_airport" title="Atlanta's second airport">
        Atlanta's second airport
       </a>
       is in the very preliminary discussion and study phase.
      </p>
      <p>
       Domestic-only carriers from Atlanta:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Alaska Airlines
       </li>
       <li>
        American Airlines
       </li>
       <li>
        Frontier Airlines
       </li>
       <li>
        Spirit Airlines
       </li>
       <li>
        United Airlines
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Domestic and international from Atlanta:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Delta Air Lines
       </li>
       <li>
        Southwest Airlines
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Foreign-based international carriers:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Air Canada
       </li>
       <li>
        Air France (Joint venture with Delta Air Lines)
       </li>
       <li>
        British Airways
       </li>
       <li>
        KLM Royal Dutch Airlines (Joint venture with Delta Air Lines)
       </li>
       <li>
        Korean Air
       </li>
       <li>
        Lufthansa German Airlines
       </li>
       <li>
        Qatar Airways
       </li>
       <li>
        Turkish Airlines
       </li>
       <li>
        Virgin Atlantic
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Other airports (maintained by local counties) include
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlie_Brown_Field" title="Charlie Brown Field">
        Charlie Brown Field
       </a>
       (Fulton),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McCollum_Field" title="McCollum Field">
        McCollum Field
       </a>
       (Cobb),
       <a href="/wiki/Cartersville_Airport" title="Cartersville Airport">
        Cartersville Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DeKalb_Peachtree_Airport" title="DeKalb Peachtree Airport">
        DeKalb Peachtree Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Briscoe_Field" title="Briscoe Field">
        Briscoe Field
       </a>
       (Gwinnett),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coweta_County_Airport" title="Coweta County Airport">
        Coweta County Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cherokee_County_Airport_(Georgia)" title="Cherokee County Airport (Georgia)">
        Cherokee County Airport
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clayton_County_Airport_-_Tara_Field" title="Clayton County Airport - Tara Field">
        Tara Field
       </a>
       (Henry), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paulding_County_Airport" title="Paulding County Airport">
        Paulding County Airport
       </a>
       in (Paulding). Former local airports were
       <a href="/wiki/Stone_Mountain_Airport" title="Stone Mountain Airport">
        Stone Mountain Airport
       </a>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Parkaire_Field&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Parkaire Field (page does not exist)">
        Parkaire Field
       </a>
       , among others.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DeKalb_Peachtree_Airport" title="DeKalb Peachtree Airport">
        DeKalb Peachtree Airport
       </a>
       is the primary business jet airport. This is due to its proximity to Downtown, Midtown, Buckhead, and the Perimeter office areas.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roads_and_freeways">
        Roads and freeways
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Atlanta_metropolitan_area&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Roads and freeways">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Atlanta is served by three major interstate highways. Including tributaries, they are the following:
      </p>
      <p>
       (Note: The cities used below are also the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Control_cities" title="Control cities">
        control cities
       </a>
       used for the Metro Atlanta Bypass/I-285 signs entering from the suburbs.)
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_75_in_Georgia" title="Interstate 75 in Georgia">
        Interstate 75
       </a>
       passes through from Macon to the south, and from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chattanooga" title="Chattanooga">
        Chattanooga
       </a>
       to the north.
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_575" title="Interstate 575">
        Interstate 575
       </a>
       is a spur which merges with I‑75 near Kennesaw. I‑575 serves northeast portions of Cobb County and a large portion of Cherokee County. It ends in Ball Ground.
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_675_(Georgia)" title="Interstate 675 (Georgia)">
        Interstate 675
       </a>
       is a route which connects I‑75 in Henry County to I‑285 in southern Dekalb County. Most of the corridor is within Clayton County.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_85_in_Georgia" title="Interstate 85 in Georgia">
        Interstate 85
       </a>
       passes through from Montgomery on the southwest and from Greenville on the northeast. I-75 merges with I-85 to form the
       <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Connector" title="Downtown Connector">
        Downtown Connector
       </a>
       from the Brookwood Interchange, just north of Midtown Atlanta, to just south of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lakewood_Freeway" title="Lakewood Freeway">
        Lakewood Freeway
       </a>
       in south Atlanta.
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_185_(Georgia)" title="Interstate 185 (Georgia)">
        Interstate 185
       </a>
       is a spur which merges with I‑85 in LaGrange and stretches southward to Columbus.
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_985" title="Interstate 985">
        Interstate 985
       </a>
       is a spur which merges with I‑85 in Suwanee and serves the northern suburbs of Gwinnett and Hall Counties. It terminates just northeast of Gainesville.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_285" title="Interstate 285">
        Interstate 285
       </a>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beltway" title="Beltway">
        beltway
       </a>
       which encircles the city and its immediate eastern suburbs. It is commonly known as the Perimeter. I‑285 passes through Clayton, Cobb, Fulton, and DeKalb Counties.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Interstate_20_in_Georgia" title="Interstate 20 in Georgia">
        Interstate 20
       </a>
       passes through from Birmingham to the west and from Augusta to the east. It serves Douglasville, the major suburb west of Atlanta. It serves Lithonia and Conyers to the east.
      </p>
      <p>
       Atlanta is also served by several other freeways, in addition to the interstate highways, including:
      </p>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_400" title="Georgia 400">
        Georgia 400
       </a>
       is the main corridor serving the north-central suburbs, and was the only toll road in the metropolitan Atlanta area. As of November 23, 2013, the tolls ended and the toll plazas are demolished. It reaches into the northern portion of Fulton County and gradually turns northeast before entering Forsyth County. The controlled-access portion terminates just northeast of the city of Cumming. To the south, it terminates and merges into southbound I‑85 just south of the Buckhead
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Business_district" title="Business district">
        business district
       </a>
       . Cumming/
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dahlonega" title="Dahlonega">
        Dahlonega
       </a>
       is used on I‑285 as the northbound sign, and Atlanta/Buckhead as the southbound. From I‑85 northbound, it uses Buckhead/Cumming.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Stone_Mountain_Freeway" title="Stone Mountain Freeway">
        Stone Mountain Freeway
       </a>
       , or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._78" title="U.S. 78">
        U.S. 78
       </a>
       , is an 8‑mile corridor east of Downtown Atlanta and the neighboring suburb of Decatur. It serves northeast portions of Dekalb County, including the city of Stone Mountain. It continues east as a divided highway into south Gwinnett County, including the suburb of Snellville. U.S. 78 also stretches east to Athens.
      </p>
      <p>
       Lakewood Freeway, or
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_State_Route_166" title="Georgia State Route 166">
        Georgia 166
       </a>
       , extends between Lakewood Park in south Atlanta and Campbellton Road, just west of I‑285.
      </p>
      <p>
       Peachtree Industrial Blvd, or
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_State_Route_141" title="Georgia State Route 141">
        Georgia 141
       </a>
       , is a route north-northeast of Atlanta which begins on the north side of I‑285 and runs parallel to I‑85 for about four miles until it terminates when it splits into GA‑141 and Peachtree Industrial (continuing as a normal divided highway).
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_State_Route_316" title="Georgia State Route 316">
        Georgia State Route 316
       </a>
       is a four-mile-long route that branches from I‑85 and stretches eastward into Gwinnett County. It continues east as a normal divided highway through the suburb of Lawrenceville and on to Athens.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are many historic roads across the area, named after
       <a href="/wiki/Historic_mills_of_the_Atlanta_area" title="Historic mills of the Atlanta area">
        its mills
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Historic_ferries_of_the_Atlanta_area" title="Historic ferries of the Atlanta area">
        early ferries
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Historic_bridges_of_the_Atlanta_area" title="Historic bridges of the Atlanta area">
        the bridges
       </a>
       later built to replace the ferries.
       <a href="/wiki/Pace%27s_Ferry" title="Pace's Ferry">
        Pace's Ferry
       </a>
       is perhaps the best known.
      </p>
      <p>
       Owing to the area's long history of settlement and uneven terrain, most
       <a href="/wiki/Arterial_road" title="Arterial road">
        arterial roads
       </a>
       are not straight but meander instead, which can be confusing as much as the famed proliferation of Atlanta streets with "Peachtree" in the name. It is also often joked that half the streets are named Peachtree, while the other half have several names to make up for it.
      </p>
      <p>
       Partly, confusion is because the region maintains the historic nomenclature of each county naming its roads for the towns they connect with in surrounding counties. Thus, from Dallas to Roswell,
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_State_Route_120" title="Georgia State Route 120">
        Georgia 120
       </a>
       is Marietta Highway to the Paulding/Cobb county line, is Dallas Highway to the city of Marietta, Whitlock Avenue to the
       <a href="/wiki/Town_square" title="Town square">
        town square
       </a>
       , South Park Square for just one
       <a href="/wiki/City_block" title="City block">
        city block
       </a>
       , Roswell Street to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cobb_Parkway" title="Cobb Parkway">
        Cobb Parkway
       </a>
       (at the
       <a href="/wiki/Big_Chicken" title="Big Chicken">
        Big Chicken
       </a>
       ), Roswell Road to the Cobb/Fulton county line, and finally Marietta Street to the town square in Roswell. Further confusion is from the arbitrary location of state routes by the
       <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Department_of_Transportation" title="Georgia Department of Transportation">
        Georgia Department of Transportation
       </a>
       (GDOT), so that they travel an erratic path requiring several turns by drivers instead of traveling the original straight route; and the renaming of roads by state legislators to honor their friends.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are many roads like this throughout the area, leading to duplication of names in different counties. In Fulton, "Roswell Road" refers to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_9" title="Georgia 9">
        Georgia 9
       </a>
       through northern Atlanta and across Sandy Springs, in addition to the above-mentioned use in Cobb, for example. Numeric
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Street_address" title="Street address">
        street addressing
       </a>
       is done by county as well, with the origin usually being at one corner of the town square in the county seat. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Postal_Service" title="U.S. Postal Service">
        U.S. Postal Service
       </a>
       ignores these actual and logical boundaries however, overlapping
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">
        ZIP codes
       </a>
       and their associated place names across counties. The Cumberland/Galleria area has Cobb's numbers and an "SE" suffix, but is called "Atlanta" by the USPS (despite being
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vinings" title="Vinings">
        Vinings
       </a>
       , which the USPS ironically calls "unacceptable"), which can confuse visitors to think it is far away in southeast Atlanta.
      </p>
      <p>
       Where more than one town in the same county has a road to the same place, the smaller towns have their own name prefixed to it, while the
       <a href="/wiki/County_seat" title="County seat">
        county seat
       </a>
       does not. The road need not go directly to the other place, but may connect through other roads. Examples include Due West Road west from Marietta, Kennesaw Due West Road southwest from Kennesaw, and Acworth Due West Road south from Acworth. Some are usually
       <a href="/wiki/Hyphen" title="Hyphen">
        hyphenated
       </a>
       , like Peachtree-Dunwoody Road, Ashford-Dunwoody Road, Chamblee-Dunwoody Road, and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chamblee-Tucker_Road&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chamblee-Tucker Road (page does not exist)">
        Chamblee-Tucker Road
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       There are also several roads named for communities which have been overwhelmed by the urban and suburban sprawl, and so are somewhat odd to newcomers. These include
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Plains,_Georgia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sandy Plains, Georgia (page does not exist)">
        Sandy Plains
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Crabapple,_Georgia" title="Crabapple, Georgia">
        Crabapple
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Toonigh,_Georgia" title="Toonigh, Georgia">
        Toonigh
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Luxomni,_Georgia" title="Luxomni, Georgia">
        Luxomni
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Due_West,_Georgia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Due West, Georgia (page does not exist)">
        Due West
       </a>
       . Some of these communities are in the middle of the road, while some are at or very near one end. Some areas are renamed, either over time (Sandy Plains gradually became "Sprayberry" when
       <a href="/wiki/Sprayberry_High_School" title="Sprayberry High School">
        Sprayberry High School
       </a>
       moved there and similarly named shopping centers popped up around it); by the USPS (Toonigh is identified as "Lebanon"), or after rapid development. In such cases, the roads usually maintain their historic names even if the neighborhoods do not.
      </p>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          The
          <b>
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">
            neutrality
           </a>
           of this article is
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">
            disputed
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Relevant discussion may be found on the
           <a href="/wiki/Talk:Atlanta_metropolitan_area##" title="Talk:Atlanta metropolitan area">
            talk page
           </a>
           . Please do not remove this message until
           <a href="/wiki/Template:POV#When_to_remove" title="Template:POV">
            conditions to do so are met
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (November 2014)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Several of these roads have become arterials, while others remain pleasant two-lane drives. Many are state roads as well, though GDOT has the habit of moving numbered routes onto other roads, without public input, and occasionally sending them through an entirely different town. State highway numbers also tend to curve around arbitrarily while their directional signs do not, rendering them useless where they indicate "north" and "south" in places the road goes east and west.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       There are also a few
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._highway" title="U.S. highway">
        U.S. highways
       </a>
       that cross the area, including
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_19_in_Georgia" title="U.S. Route 19 in Georgia">
        19
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_23_in_Georgia" title="U.S. Route 23 in Georgia">
        23
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_29_in_Georgia" title="U.S. Route 29 in Georgia">
        29
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Route_41_in_Georgia" title="U.S. Route 41 in Georgia">
        41
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/U.S._Route_78_in_Georgia" title="U.S. Route 78 in Georgia">
        78
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Other arterials are completely new, like much of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barrett_Parkway" title="Barrett Parkway">
        Barrett Parkway
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/South_Fulton_Parkway" title="South Fulton Parkway">
        South Fulton Parkway
       </a>
       , both constructed by their counties but partly covered with a state route number. Occasionally, roads are realigned or extended to meet each other directly at a cross-road, leading to odd curves and name changes.
      </p>
